قوله : والنجم؛ عند قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في آخره : ( فَاسْجُدُوا لِلَّهِ وَاعْبُدُوا ) [النجم:62]
وانشقت، واقرأ
قوله : وانشقت؛ عند قوله : ( فَمَا لَهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ وَإِذَا قُرِئَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْءَانُ لَا يَسْجُدُونَ ) [الانشقاق:20-21]
وقوله: اقرأ؛ عند قوله: ( كَلَّا لَا تُطِعْهُ وَاسْجُدْ وَاقْتَرِبْ ) [العلق:19]
وعند الشَّافِعِي في أربع عشرة أيضاً، ففي ص عنده ليس سجدة، وفي الحج عنده سجدتان.
وعند مالك ليس في النجم وانشقت وأقرأ سجدة، والأحاديث الصحيحة في الصحاح تردّ عليه.
قوله : عنده ليس سجدة؛ لقول ابن عباس : سجدة ص ليست من عزائم السجود، وقد رأيت النبي لم يسجد فيها، أخرجه الشيخان. ولنا : الأخذ بفعل النبي، ويحمل قول ابن عباس على أنه ليس مما أمر به على سبيل العزم والقطع كما في سائر السجدات.
Al-Furqan, An-Naml, Alif Lam Mim As-Sajda, Saad, Ha Mim As-Sajda, An-Najm. He said: Al-Furqan: at His saying: 'And when it is said to them, prostrate to the Most Merciful...' [Furqan:59]. He said: An-Naml: at His saying: '[That] they do not prostrate to Allah...' [Naml:25-26]. He said: Alif Lam Mim As-Sajda: at His saying: 'Only those believe in Our verses who, when they are reminded of them, fall down in prostration...' [Sajda:15]. He said: Saad: at His saying: 'And he fell down bowing and turned in repentance' [Saad:24], and it is said at the end: 'So We forgave him that; and indeed, for him is nearness with Us and a good place of return' [Saad:25]; that is the most preponderant. He said: Ha Mim As-Sajda: and there is a difference of opinion regarding the location of the prostration in Ha Mim As-Sajda. According to Ali, it is His saying: 'If it is He whom you worship' [Fussilat:37], and Shafi'i adopted this. According to Ibn Mas'ud, it is His saying: 'And they are not arrogant' [Fussilat:38]. So we adopted this as a precaution, because delaying the prostration is permissible but advancing it is not. He said: An-Najm: at the end, according to the Prophet's saying: 'So prostrate to Allah and worship' [Najm:62]. And Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. He said: Inshiqaq: at His saying: 'So what is with them that they do not believe, and when the Quran is recited to them, they do not prostrate?' [Inshiqaq:20-21]. And Iqra': at His saying: 'No! Do not obey him. But prostrate and draw near' [Alaq:19]. And according to Shafi'i, it is also fourteen. So according to him, Saad is not a prostration, and in Hajj there are two prostrations. And according to Malik, there is no prostration in An-Najm, Inshiqaq, and Iqra', and the authentic hadiths in the sound books refute him. He said: According to him, it is not a prostration because of the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'The prostration in Saad is not among the assiduous prostrations, and I saw the Prophet did not prostrate in it,' reported by Bukhari and Muslim. And our proof: taking the action of the Prophet, and the saying of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as meaning that it is not commanded with determination and decisiveness as in other prostrations.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive statement of the Hanafi school's list of verses that require sajda tilawah (prostration of recitation), along with the specific verses for each surah, and a discussion of the differences with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The Hanafi school counts fourteen prostrations: they include Surah Saad, while Shafi'i considers it a prostration of thanks (shukr), not an obligatory one. In Surah Al-Hajj, Shafi'i counts two prostrations, while Hanafi counts only one (the first verse) and the second is considered a prayer prostration as explained in the previous lesson. For Surah Fussilat (Ha-Mim), there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) considers the prostration at verse 37, while Ibn Mas'ud considers it at verse 38. The Hanafi school follows Ibn Mas'ud's view as a precaution, because it is permissible to delay a wajib act but not to advance it. The Maliki school denies prostrations in An-Najm, Inshiqaq, and Iqra', but the Hanafi school relies on authentic hadiths to support their inclusion. The proof for including Saad is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did prostrate in it, and the statement of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as meaning it is not from the 'azaim (firmly obligated ones) along with others, but it is still a sajda tilawah. The Hanafi school gives precedence to the action of the Prophet over the statement of a companion.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses.
عزائم السجود (azaim al-sujud): The firmly obligated prostrations (i.e., those that are definitely wajib).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Surah Saad included among the verses of sajda tilawah even though Ibn Abbas said the Prophet did not prostrate in it?
A) Because the Hanafi school rejects the report of Ibn Abbas
B) Because the Hanafi school takes the action of the Prophet over the statement of Ibn Abbas
C) Because the Hanafi school considers Saad a prostration of thanks, not tilawah
D) Because the Hanafi school follows the view of Ali in this matter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi list of sajda tilawah verses is derived by prioritising the Prophet's action over companions' statements and applying the precaution principle, resulting in fourteen specific verses that differ slightly from other schools.

Disputed Sajdas: Surah Sad and Surah Fussilat in the Hanafi School
Inter-madhhab dispute on two sajda locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sajda in Surah Sad and the location of the sajda in Surah Fussilat, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments using the proofs cited.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that Surah Sad has a wajib sajda and the sajda in Surah Fussilat is at verse 38, based on caution and the Prophet's practice.

Sajdat al-tilawa is an important act in recitation, but the exact verses requiring prostration differ among the schools. This lesson focuses on two key disputes: whether Surah Sad contains a sajda, and where in Surah Fussilat the sajda occurs. Understanding these disagreements clarifies the Hanafi methodology of preferring caution and the interpretation of Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on disputed sajdas
From the passage, extract that the Hanafi school counts fourteen sajdas, includes Surah Sad, and places the sajda in Surah Fussilat at verse 38. Note the school's reliance on caution.
The matn states these rulings; the commentary explains the reasoning.
2
Examine the Shafi'i counter-position and its proof
The Shafi'i school argues Surah Sad has no sajda (citing Ibn 'Abbas) and places the Fussilat sajda at verse 24 (citing 'Ali). Identify their primary dalil: the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas.
The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response interprets Ibn 'Abbas's statement to mean the sajda is not a 'determined obligation' (azima) but still wajib. The reliance on the Prophet's actual practice in other sajdas is the Hanafi proof.
The commentary states: 'we act upon the action of the Prophet'.
4
Understand the principle of caution (ihtiyat)
For Surah Fussilat, the Hanafi school adopts Ibn Mas'ud's placement (verse 38) out of caution, because delaying a sajda is permissible but advancing it is not. This is a distinctive Hanafi method.
The textual basis: 'fa akhadhnā bihā iḥtiyāṭan, fa inna taʼkhīr al-sajdah jāʼiz lā taqdīmah'.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis prostrate for Surah Sad and at verse 38 of Fussilat; Shafi'is do not prostrate for Sad and prostrate at verse 24 of Fussilat. This affects both prayer and tilawa settings.
Knowing this distinction prevents confusion when following different imams or studying across schools.

Book of Prayer / Prostration of Recitation. And [Surah] al-Inshiqaq, and [Surah] Iqra', or he heard it even if he did not intend. And according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) there are also fourteen [sajdas]; so in Surah Sad according to him there is no sajdah, and in Surah al-Hajj according to him there are two sajdahs. And they differed concerning the place of the sajdah in Surah Ha Mim al-Sajdah: according to 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) it is His statement: 'If you are worshipping Him' and al-Shafi'i adopted this; and according to Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) it is His statement: 'And they do not become arrogant'. [1] His statement: 'al-Inshiqaq'; at His statement: 'So what is the matter with them that they do not believe, and when the Quran is recited to them they do not prostrate?' [2] His statement: 'and according to al-Shafi'i' and according to Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) there is no sajdah in [Surah] al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra', and the authentic hadiths in the Sahihs refute him. Our proof: acting upon the action of the Prophet, and the saying of Ibn 'Abbas is interpreted to mean that it is not commanded with determination and decisiveness like other sajdas. [4] His statement: 'out of caution' because delaying an obligatory act beyond its time, especially if it is permissive, is permissible, and it is not permissible to advance it before its time.

Commentary
This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya is a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya dealing with the subject of sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation). It opens by clarifying the Hanafi position on which verses require prostration, then presents inter-madhhab disputes. The matn states that sajda is required in Surah al-Inshiqaq and Surah al-'Alaq (Iqra'), and also for one who hears the verse even without intending. The commentator notes that al-Shafi'i counts fourteen sajdas, but differs on Surah Sad (no sajda) and has two in Surah al-Hajj. The Hanafi school, however, follows the position of Ibn Mas'ud for Surah Fussilat, taking the later verse (verse 38) as the sajda, out of caution since delaying a sajda is permissible but not advancing it. The commentary then provides proofs: for Surah al-Inshiqaq, the verse is cited; the Maliki view denying sajda in certain surahs is refuted by authentic hadiths; the Shafi'i proof from Ibn 'Abbas that Surah Sad has no sajda is countered by the Hanafi argument following the Prophet's actual practice, understanding Ibn 'Abbas's statement to mean it is not a determined (azima) obligation like other sajdas. Finally, the cautionary principle is explained: an wajib can be delayed within its permissive time but cannot be performed before its time.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command to prostrate.
عزائم السجود (ʻazāʼim al-sujūd): The determined or strongly established prostrations, implying a higher degree of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that Surah Sad has a wajib sajda and the sajda in Surah Fussilat is at verse 38, based on caution and the Prophet's practice.

Rulings for Imam, Muqtadi, and External Listener in Sajdat al-Tilawa
Specifies who must prostrate when a sajda verse is recited in different contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for each participant (imam, muqtadi, external listener) when a sajda verse is recited, identify the condition of intent for hearing, and apply the Hanafi position with its proof.

Core Idea
The muqtadi follows the imam in sajdat al-tilawa; his own recitation is void; the external listener prostrates after prayer.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah details the obligations for sajdat al-tilawa when a sajda verse is recited in different contexts within congregational prayer. It clarifies the roles of the imam, the follower (muqtadi), and a listener outside the prayer, and introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether intention to listen is required for the obligation to prostrate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three participants
List the three categories: the imam who recites the sajda verse, the muqtadi following the imam, and the external listener (sami' khariji) who hears the verse from someone in prayer but is not part of that prayer.
The external listener may be praying alone or not in prayer at all.
2
State the ruling for each participant
For the imam: he prostrates and the muqtadi prostrates with him. For the muqtadi: if he himself recites a sajda verse, he does not prostrate at all. For the external listener: he prostrates after the prayer, not during it.
The muqtadi must prostrate even if he did not hear the verse.
3
Analyze the condition of intent for hearing
According to Abu Hanifa, the obligation to prostrate upon hearing a sajda verse is conditional upon intending to listen. Abu Yusuf holds it obligatory absolutely. Identify which view is the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa's).
The text uses 'عنده' (according to him) for Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Examine the proof and underlying principles
The hadith 'إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به' (The imam is only appointed to be followed) is cited to prove the muqtadi must follow the imam in prostration. The principle of 'hajr 'an al-qira'ah' (prevention from recitation) explains why the muqtadi's recitation is considered void.
The hadith has zanni thubut and dalala, yet it is relied upon for this ruling.

(أو سمعها وإن لم يقصده) : أي السماع
[0]قوله : أو سمعها ؛ عطف على قوله: تلاها ؛ أي يجب على من سمع آيةً يتلوها غيره بشرط أن يكون سماعه مع قصد الاستماع أو لا، لكن إذا لم يقصد لا يجب عنده، وعند أبي يوسف يجب مطلقاً.
تلا الإمام سجدَ المؤتم معه، وإن تلا المؤتم لم يسجد أصلاً، وسجد وإن لم يسمع ، السامع الخارجي سَمِعَ المصلي ممن ليس معه ، سجد بعدها، ولو سجد فيها أعادها لا الصلاة.

(Or he heard it even if he did not intend it): i.e., hearing. [0] His statement: 'or he heard it' is a conjunction to his statement: 'he recited it'; i.e., it is obligatory upon the one who hears a verse that is recited by someone else, provided that his hearing is with the intention of listening or not, but if he did not intend, it is not obligatory according to him; according to Abu Yusuf it is obligatory absolutely. The imam recited, the muqtadi prostrates with him, and if the muqtadi recited, he does not prostrate at all, and he prostrates even if he does not hear. The external listener who heard the prayer from someone not with him prostrates after it, and if he prostrates during it, he repeats the prostration, not the prayer. [1] His statement: 'prostrates' – the hadith indicates it: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed', narrated by Abu Dawood and others. [2] His statement: 'and if the muqtadi recited' – i.e., if the follower recited a verse of sajda, it is not obligatory upon him, neither in his prayer nor outside it, nor upon his imam or another follower if he heard it from him, because the follower is prevented from recitation, so his recitation is like no recitation. [3] His statement: 'and the external listener prostrates' – i.e., a person who hears the verse of sajda from the muqtadi while he is outside his prayer, not being an imam nor a follower, whether he is praying or not, because the prevenience was established for the follower, and in the imam's prostration the subject would be inverted, and that is absent in the case of the external person. [4] His statement: 'the one praying' – whether he is an imam, a muqtadi, or a munfarid, and likewise whoever hears from him in general, whether he is an imam other than his imam, or a muqtadi with that imam, or a munfarid, or not praying at all. [0] His statement: 'and if he prostrated' – i.e., if he prostrated that prostration during his prayer, it does not suffice him because it is incomplete; because the command to complete the pillar he is in, and moving to another entails prohibition of occupying with performing something that became obligatory due to an external cause in the prayer, so the complete one is not achieved, and he repeats that prostration, and he is not obligated to repeat the entire prayer, because an addition of less than a rak'ah does not invalidate.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on sajdat al-tilawa, now focusing on the obligations of different participants in congregational prayer. It first clarifies the condition for obligation upon hearing: according to the preferred Hanafi view (Imam Abu Hanifa), if one hears a sajda verse without intending to listen, it is not obligatory (wajib). Abu Yusuf holds it obligatory absolutely. The later part gives the key ruling: when the imam recites a sajda verse, the muqtadi must prostrate with him, even if he did not hear the verse. If the muqtadi himself recites a sajda verse (e.g., in a silent prayer or behind an imam), he does not prostrate at all, neither during nor after the prayer, because his recitation is invalid due to being forbidden (mamnu). A listener outside the prayer who hears the muqtadi must prostrate after the prayer, not during it. If someone prostrates during the prayer for an external sajda, that prostration is invalid and must be repeated after the prayer, but the prayer itself remains valid because adding less than a rak'ah does not nullify it. The proofs are given: the hadith 'the imam is to be followed' for the muqtadi's obligation; the principle that the muqtadi's recitation is like no recitation; the prevention (hajr) applies to the muqtadi only.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-muʼtamm): The person following the imam in congregational prayer (the muqtadi).
السامع الخارجي (al-sāmiʻ al-khārijī): A person who hears the sajda verse from someone praying but is himself not part of that prayer (not the imam, not the muqtadi).
حجر عن القراءة (ḥajr ʻan al-qirāʼah): The prevention or prohibition of recitation for the muqtadi behind the imam; their recitation is considered invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must prostrate when the imam recites a sajda verse; the muqtadi's own recitation is void, so no prostration is due; an external listener prostrates after the prayer, with the condition of intent according to the mufta bihi view.

Sajdah al-Tilawah: Imam, Follower, and External Listener
Rulings on prostration of recitation in and out of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for sajdah al-tilawah in congregational prayer for the imam, follower, and external listener, and explain the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
The follower's prostration is tied to the imam; his own recitation is irrelevant; external listener prostrates after prayer.

This lesson examines a set of rulings from the Hanafi school regarding sajdah al-tilawah when it occurs during congregational prayer. The passage, a commentary on a base text, clarifies the obligations of the imam, the follower (muqtadi), and a person who is not part of that prayer (the external listener). It also discusses the effect of timing—whether the listener joins the imam's rak'ah or another—and the relationship between sajdah al-tilawah and the prayer's own bowing and prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parties
Understand the roles: imam (reciter), follower (muqtadi), and external listener (anyone not engaged in that specific prayer). Each has a different ruling.
The passage distinguishes between 'sāmi‘ khārijī' and those inside the prayer.
2
Apply the general rule: prostration follows the imam
When the imam recites a sajdah verse, every follower must prostrate with him, even if they did not hear the verse. Proof: hadith 'إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به' (The imam is appointed to be followed).
3
Handle the follower's own recitation
If the follower recites a sajdah verse, he does not prostrate at all—neither inside nor outside the prayer. His recitation is considered invalid (mahjur) because he is forbidden to recite behind the imam in a loud prayer. Likewise, the imam and other followers do not prostrate upon hearing it.
This is because the follower's recitation is legally nonexistent.
4
Determine the ruling for the external listener
An external listener who hears a sajdah verse from someone praying (imam, follower, or alone) must prostrate after the prayer, not during it. If he prostrates during his own prayer, that prostration is invalid and must be repeated, but his prayer remains valid.
The prostration is wajib upon hearing, but the prayer context restricts its timing.
5
Consider timing and the prayer's sujud
If the external listener joins the imam in the same rak'ah before the imam prostrates, he prostrates with him. If he joins later or in another rak'ah, he prostrates after finishing his prayer. Also, a sajdah tilawah that occurs during prayer is normally discharged by the prayer's ruku' and sujud if there is no gap of three verses between recitation and bowing.
This nuance arises from the principle that the prayer's own sujud suffices when contiguous.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(٤) قوله : المصلي؛ سواء كان إماماً أو مؤتماً أو منفرداً، وكذا من سمع منه عام من أن يكون إماماً غير إمامه، أو مؤتماً بذلك الإمام، أو منفرداً أو غير مصل أصلاً.
[0]قوله : ولو سجد؛ أي لو سجد تلك السَّجدة في صلاته لم تجزه؛ لأنها ناقصة؛ لأنَّ الأمر بإتمام الركن الذي هو فيه، وانتقاله إلى آخر يقتضي النَّهي عن الاشتغال بأداء ما وجب بسبب خارج عن الصَّلاةِ فيها، فلا يتأدى بها الكامل، وأعاد تلك السَّجدة، ولا تجب عليه إعادة الصَّلاةِ بتمامها؛ لأنّ زيادةً ما دونَ الرَّكعةِ لا تفسد
سمعها من إمام، ولم يدخل معه، أو دخل في ركعةٍ أُخرى سَجَدَ لا فيها، وإن دَخَلَ في تلك الركعة إن كان قبل سجودِ إمامِهِ سَجَدَ معه، والا لا يسجد، والسجدة الصلاتية لا تُقضَى خارجها
[١]قوله : سجد؛ بعدها؛ أي بعد الفراغ عن الصَّلاة، هذا إذا ائتم به في الركعة الأخرى؛ لأن الواجب خارج الصَّلاة لا يقضى في الصَّلاة، وإذا لم يدخل معه فأداؤها ظاهر، ولعلك تفطنت من هاهنا ما في كلامه من المسامحة، ولو قال: سجد خارجها لكان أولى.
[٢]قوله : وإلا لا يسجد؛ لأنه صار مدركاً لها بإدراك تلك الركعة.
[٣] قوله : لا تُقضى؛ بصيغة المجهول، أي لا تؤدى فإنَّ القضاء يستعمل بمعنى الأداء، كما في قوله تعالى: فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلَوةُ فَانتَشِرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ.
(٤) قوله : خارجها؛ قد يقال : إن سجدة التلاوة في الصَّلاةِ تتأدى بركوع وسجود صلبي عندنا فلا تبقى عليه حتى تؤدى خارج الصلاة. ويجاب عنه : بأنَّ هذا إنَّما هو إذا ركع وسجد بعد قراءة آية السجدة متصلاً من غير فصل بقدر ثلاث آيات، وأما إذا كان فصل، فلا تتأدى تلك السجدة بالركوع والسجود، فيلزم أن يبين حكمها هل تؤدى خارج الصَّلاةِ أم لا؟ والوجه في عدم أدائها خارج الصَّلاةِ أنَّ السَّجدة الصلوتية وجوبها كامل، ولها مزية الصَّلاة، ألا ترى أنه لو ضحك في سجدةِ التَّلاوة في الصلاة تنتقض طهارته، ولو ضحك فيها خارج الصَّلاةِ لا تنتقض، فتكون لها مزية فلا تتأدى بالناقص.
[0] قوله : خارج الصَّلاة؛ سواء كان خارج الصَّلاةِ مطلقاً أو في صلاة أخرى.
If the imam recites, the follower prostrates with him, even if he did not hear. And if the follower recites, he does not prostrate at all: i.e., neither in the prayer nor after it. And the external listener, who hears the praying person from among those not with him, prostrates after it. And if he prostrates during it, he repeats it but not the prayer. The prostration is required even if he did not intend to hear it, due to the saying of Ibn 'Umar: 'Prostration is upon the one who hears it' (recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah). [1] His saying: 'prostrates' – the hadith 'The imam is appointed only to be followed' indicates it, recorded by Abu Dawud and others. [2] His saying: 'And if the follower recites' – i.e., if the follower recites a verse of prostration, it is not obligatory upon him, neither in his prayer nor outside it, nor upon his imam nor upon another follower who hears it from him, because the follower is prevented from reciting, so his recitation is as if no recitation. (3) His saying: 'And the external listener prostrates' – i.e., one who hears from the follower a verse of prostration while he is outside his prayer, not being an imam nor a follower, whether he is praying or not, because the prevention is established in respect of the follower, and in the prostration of the imam it would necessitate reversing the subject, which is absent in the case of the external person. (4) His saying: 'the praying person' – whether he is an imam, a follower, or one praying alone, and likewise anyone who hears from him generally, whether he is an imam other than his own imam, or a follower of that imam, or alone, or not praying at all. [0] His saying: 'And if he prostrates' – i.e., if he prostrates that prostration during his prayer, it does not suffice him because it is deficient; because the command is to complete the pillar he is in, and moving to another entails prohibition of engaging in performing what is obligatory due to something external to the prayer within it, so the complete act is not thereby performed, and he repeats that prostration, and he does not have to repeat the entire prayer because an increase of less than a rak'ah does not invalidate. He heard it from an imam and did not enter with him, or entered in another rak'ah – he prostrates after it. And if he entered in that same rak'ah, if it was before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him; otherwise he does not prostrate. And the prayer-related prostration is not performed outside it. [1] His saying: 'prostrates after it' – i.e., after finishing the prayer; this is when he followed him in another rak'ah because the obligation outside the prayer is not performed in the prayer. And if he did not enter with him, performing it is apparent. And perhaps you have realized from here what is in his words of leniency, and if he said 'he prostrates outside it' it would be better. [2] His saying: 'otherwise he does not prostrate' – because he has caught up with it by catching up with that rak'ah. [3] His saying: 'is not performed' in the passive voice – i.e., it is not performed, for 'qada' is used in the sense of performance, as in the verse: 'And when the prayer is finished, then disperse in the land'. (4) His saying: 'outside it' – it may be said: The prostration of recitation in the prayer is performed by the bowing and prostration of the prayer according to us, so it does not remain upon him to be performed outside the prayer. And it is answered: This is only if he bows and prostrates after reciting the verse of prostration consecutively without a gap of three verses. But if there is a gap, that prostration is not performed by the bowing and prostration, so it becomes necessary to clarify its ruling: is it performed outside the prayer or not? And the reason for not performing it outside the prayer is that the obligation of the prayer-related prostration is complete, and it has the merit of the prayer. Do you not see that if he laughs during the prostration of recitation in the prayer, his purification is invalidated; but if he laughs during it outside the prayer, it is not invalidated. Thus it has a merit, so it is not performed by the deficient. [0] His saying: 'outside the prayer' – whether entirely outside the prayer or in another prayer.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of sajdah al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) in the context of congregational prayer. It addresses multiple scenarios. First, if the imam recites a verse of sajdah, every follower must prostrate with him, even if they did not hear the verse. This is based on the hadith that the imam is appointed to be followed, and on the principle that the follower's prostration is linked to the imam's recitation. Second, if the follower himself recites a verse of sajdah during prayer, he does not prostrate at all—neither in the prayer nor outside it—because the follower is prohibited from reciting behind the imam; his recitation is legally considered non-existent. Third, a person who is not engaged in that prayer (an external listener) who hears a sajdah verse from someone praying must prostrate after the prayer, not during it. If he prostrates during the prayer, his prostration is invalid and he must repeat it, but his prayer remains valid because adding less than a rak'ah does not invalidate the prayer. The proof for these rulings includes the statement of Ibn 'Umar that 'prostration is upon the one who hears it' and the general principle of following the imam. The commentary also discusses the case of someone who hears a sajdah from an imam but does not join that imam, or joins in a later rak'ah—such a person prostrates after finishing his own prayer. If he joins the same rak'ah before the imam prostrates, he prostrates with the imam; otherwise he does not. Finally, the text clarifies that a sajdah of tilawah that occurs during prayer is normally discharged by the ruku' and sujud of the prayer itself, provided there is no lengthy gap (three verses) between reciting the sajdah verse and bowing. If a gap occurs, the sajdah remains due but is not performed outside the prayer because it has the special merit of being part of the prayer; for example, laughing during sajdah al-tilawah in prayer invalidates wudu, but laughing outside prayer does not. Thus the sajdah cannot be performed deficiently outside the prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command of prostration.
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
السامع الخارجي (al-sāmi‘ al-khārijī): A person who is not engaged in the same prayer as the reciter, i.e., not the imam nor a follower of that imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower (muqtadi) recites a verse of sajdah during the prayer, what is the ruling?
A) He must prostrate immediately.
B) He does not prostrate at all, neither in the prayer nor outside it.
C) He prostrates after the prayer.
D) He prostrates and repeats his prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower's prostration is contingent on the imam; his own recitation has no effect. External listeners prostrate after prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Prayer Prostration Is Not Performed Outside Prayer: Principle and Proof
Ruling with proof: sajda due in prayer is not performed outside.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sajdat al-tilawa that becomes due during prayer is not performed outside prayer, and explain the linguistic proof from the Quran.

Core Idea
The obligation of a prayer-based sajda lapses if not performed during the prayer; it is not made up later.

In the Hanafi school, sajdat al-tilawa is wajib. However, when the prostration is triggered within the prayer, it acquires a special status: it must be performed inside the prayer, and if missed, it is not performed outside. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its Quranic support, and addresses an important intra-madhhab disagreement about repetition after the salutation.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the exact ruling from the passage: 'السجدة الصلاتية لا تُقضى خارجها' means the prostration due in prayer is not performed outside of it.
The term 'قضى' here means 'performed', not 'made up'.
2
Examine the Quranic Proof
The author cites Surah al-Jumu'ah (62:10) where 'قُضِيَت' means 'performed' (ليس القضاء بمعنى الفوات بل بمعنى الأداء). This supports that 'لا تقضى' means 'not performed'.
This is a linguistic proof (dalil laghawi).
3
Respond to the Objection
An objection arises: in prayer, the regular ruk'u and sujud may fulfill the sajda. The answer: only if done immediately without a gap of three verses; otherwise, it must be performed as a separate sajda, but still cannot be done outside prayer.
The privilege of prayer makes the sajda stronger; laughter nullifies wudu inside prayer but not outside.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
If one recites a sajda verse in prayer, prostrates, then after salam recites the same verse again, some scholars say another prostration is wajib, others say no. The correct view (al-sahih) is that if the person spoke between recitations, it is wajib; otherwise not.
Speech breaks the continuity of the session (majlis).
5
Consider the Practical Consequence
If a sajda is missed during prayer, the obligation lapses; one does not perform it after prayer. This is the mufta bihi position.
Only if the sajda was due solely in prayer; if it was due before entering prayer, different rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة / سجود التلاوة. سمعها من إمام، ولم يدخل معه، أو دخل في ركعةٍ أُخرى سَجَدَ لا فيها، وإن دَخَلَ في تلك الركعة إن كان قبل سجودِ إمامِهِ سَجَدَ معه، والا لا يسجد، والسجدة الصلاتية لا تُقضَى خارجها. سمعها من إمام، ولم يدخل معه، أو دخل في ركعة أُخرى سَجَدَ لا فيها، وإن دَخَلَ في تلك الركعة إن كان: أي الدخول قبل سجودِ إمامِهِ سَجَدَ معه، والا لا يسجد. والسجدة الصلاتية لا تُقْضَى خارجها: أي سجدة التلاوة التي محلها الصلاة لا تُقضَى خارج الصلاة إلا إذا تابع المصلي التالي فتفسد لمتابعة غير إمامه، ولا تجزئه عما سمع. [١]قوله: سجد بعدها؛ أي بعد الفراغ عن الصَّلاة، هذا إذا ائتم به في الركعة الأخرى؛ لأن الواجب خارج الصَّلاة لا يقضى في الصَّلاة، وإذا لم يدخل معه فأداؤها ظاهر. [٢]قوله: وإلا لا يسجد؛ لأنه صار مدركاً لها بإدراك تلك الركعة. [٣] قوله: لا تُقضى؛ بصيغة المجهول، أي لا تؤدى فإنَّ القضاء يستعمل بمعنى الأداء، كما في قوله: فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلَوةُ فَانتَشِرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ. (٤) قوله: خارجها؛ قد يقال: إن سجدة التلاوة في الصَّلاةِ تتأدى بركوع وسجود صلبي عندنا فلا تبقى عليه حتى تؤدى خارج الصلاة. ويجاب عنه: بأنَّ هذا إنَّما هو إذا ركع وسجد بعد قراءة آية السجدة متصلاً من غير فصل بقدر ثلاث آيات، وأما إذا كان فصل، فلا تتأدى تلك السجدة بالركوع والسجود، فيلزم أن يبين حكمها هل تؤدى خارج الصَّلاةِ أم لا؟ والوجه في عدم أدائها خارج الصَّلاةِ أنَّ السَّجدة الصلوتية وجوبها كامل، ولها مزية الصَّلاة، ألا ترى أنه لو ضحك في سجدةِ التَّلاوة في الصلاة تنتقض طهارته، ولو ضحك فيها خارج الصَّلاةِ لا تنتقض، فتكون لها مزية فلا تتأدى بالناقص. [0] قوله: خارج الصَّلاة؛ سواء كان خارج الصَّلاةِ مطلقاً أو في صلاة أخرى. تلاها ثم شرع في الصلاة، وأعاد، كفته سجدة، وإن تلاها وسجد، ثم شرع فيها وأعادَ سَجَدَ أُخرى؛ لأنَّ في الصُّورة الأولى غير الصلاتية صارت تبعاً للصلاتية. [١] قوله: احتراز... الخ حاصله: أنه لو قلنا: وجبت في الصلاة يدخل فيها السجدة التي تجب في الصَّلاة، ومحل أدائها خارجها، كما إذا سمع المصلي ممن ليس معه، فيلزم أن تؤدى خارج الصَّلاة، مع أنه يلزم أداؤها خارجها. [٢] قوله: أو سمع من إمامه؛ أطلق لفظ الإمام باعتبار ما يؤول إليه، وإلا فهو ليس بإمـام له عندما سمعه منه. [٣] قوله: شرع... الخ؛ وفي عكسه؛ وهو ما إذا تلاها في الصَّلاةِ فسجد ثم أعادها بعد السلام، قيل: تجب أخرى، وقيل: لا، ووفق بينهما كحمل الأول على ما إذا تكلم؛ لأن الكلام يقطعُ حكم المجلس، والثاني على ما إذا لم يتكلم، وهذا هو الصحيح. [٤]قوله: وأعاد؛ أي قرأ تلك الآيةَ مرَّة أُخرى في الصلاة، فإن قرأ فيها آية أُخرى وجبت سجدة أخرى. [0] قوله: لأن... الخ؛ حاصله: أنَّ في الصورة الأولى، وهي ما إذا قرأ آية السجدة خارج الصَّلاة، ثم شرع في الصَّلاة وأعادها السجدة الأولى غير صلاتية، والثانية صلاتية، والأولى ناقصة بالنسبة إلى الثانية، وكون القوية الكاملة مستبعة للناقصة ممكن، فتصير الأولى تبعاً للثانية، وتتأدى بأدائها، وهذا كله على ظاهر الرواية.
Book of Prayer / Prostration of Recitation. He heard it from an imam and did not enter with him, or entered in another rak'ah, he prostrates not in it. And if he entered in that rak'ah, if it was before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him; otherwise he does not prostrate. The prayer prostration is not performed outside of it. He heard it from an imam and did not enter with him, or entered in another rak'ah, he prostrates not in it. And if he entered in that rak'ah, if the entry was before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him; otherwise he does not prostrate. 'The prayer prostration is not performed outside of it' means the prostration of recitation whose place is the prayer is not performed outside the prayer except if the praying person follows the reciter, then it is invalid due to following other than his imam, and it does not suffice him for what he heard. [1] His saying: 'he prostrates after it' means after finishing the prayer; this is if he followed him in the other rak'ah because the obligation outside prayer is not performed in prayer, and if he did not enter with him, its performance is apparent. [2] His saying: 'otherwise he does not prostrate' because he became a perceiver of it by perceiving that rak'ah. [3] His saying: 'is not performed' in the passive form, i.e., it is not done, for 'qada' is used in the meaning of 'ada', as in His saying: 'And when the prayer is concluded, disperse in the land'. [4] His saying: 'outside of it' it may be said: the prostration of recitation in prayer is fulfilled by the bowing and prostration of the prayer according to us, so it does not remain upon him to be performed outside prayer. The answer is: this is only if he bowed and prostrated immediately after reciting the verse of prostration without a gap of the length of three verses; but if there was a gap, then that prostration is not fulfilled by bowing and prostrating, so it is necessary to clarify its ruling: is it performed outside prayer or not? And the reason for not performing it outside prayer is that the prayer prostration has a complete obligation and has the privilege of prayer. Do you not see that if one laughs in the prostration of recitation in prayer, his ablution is nullified, but if he laughs in it outside prayer, it is not nullified? So it has a privilege, so it is not fulfilled by the deficient. [0] His saying: 'outside of it' includes both outside prayer absolutely or in another prayer. He recited it then entered into prayer and repeated it, one prostration suffices him; but if he recited it and prostrated, then entered into it and repeated it, he prostrates another because in the first case, the non-prayer one becomes a follower of the prayer one. [1] His saying: 'caution...' its summary is: if we say: 'it became obligatory in prayer', it includes the prostration that becomes obligatory in prayer and its place of performance is outside it, as when a praying person hears from someone not with him, then it would be necessary to perform it outside prayer, even though it is necessary to perform it outside it. [2] His saying: 'or heard from his imam' he used the term imam considering its ultimate outcome, otherwise he is not his imam when he heard from him. [3] His saying: 'entered...' and its opposite: when one recites it in prayer and prostrates, then repeats it after greeting: it is said another is obligatory, and it is said no; and reconciliation between them is made by carrying the first on the case where he spoke, because speech cuts the ruling of the session, and the second on the case where he did not speak, and this is the correct one. [4] His saying: 'and repeated' means he read that verse another time in prayer, for if he read another verse in it, another prostration becomes obligatory. [0] His saying: 'because...' its summary: in the first case, which is when one reads the verse of prostration outside prayer, then enters prayer and repeats it, the first prostration is non-prayer and the second is prayer, and the first is deficient relative to the second, and it is possible that the strong complete one subsumes the deficient, so the first becomes a follower of the second and is performed by its performance; and all this is according to the apparent transmission.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on rulings related to sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) when it is heard from an imam, and the distinction between prostration performed inside prayer versus outside. The text explains that if a person hears a verse of prostration from an imam but does not join his prayer, or joins in a different rak'ah, he should not prostrate within that rak'ah. However, if he joins that rak'ah before the imam performs the prostration, he prostrates with him. The key principle is that a prostration that was supposed to be performed in prayer is not made up outside of it. This is supported by the Quranic usage where 'qada' means 'to perform' (Surah al-Jumu'ah, ayah 10). The commentary addresses an objection that in prayer, the prostration of recitation is fulfilled by the regular bowing and prostration (ruk'u and sujud) and thus does not need to be performed outside. The response distinguishes this: it is only fulfilled if the worshiper bows and prostrates immediately after reciting the verse without a gap of more than three verses; otherwise, it is not fulfilled, and the ruling stands that it is not performed outside. The reasoning is that the prayer prostration has a complete obligation and the privilege of prayer (as shown by laughter nullifying ablution in prayer but not outside), so it cannot be performed with a deficient act like an outside prostration. The passage also covers a scenario: if someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer, then enters prayer and recites the same verse again, one prostration suffices because the outside one becomes subsidiary to the prayer one. But if he recites and prostrates outside, then in prayer recites again, he must perform another prostration because the outside one was already performed and cannot be merged. There is a noted disagreement (ikhtilaf) about the reverse case: if he recites in prayer, prostrates, then after salutation recites again; some say another prostration is required, others say not. The reconciliation is based on whether he spoke between recitations, which changes the ruling of the session. The text concludes that these rulings are on the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah).

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran.
السجدة الصلاتية (al-sajdah al-ṣalātiyyah): The sajdat al-tilawa that becomes due within the prayer.
قضى (qaḍā): Used in the sense of 'to perform' (أدى) in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic proof that 'لا تُقضى' means 'not performed' rather than 'not made up'?
A) The hadith 'قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم'
B) The Quranic verse 'فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلَوةُ' where 'قُضِيَت' means 'performed'
C) The consensus of scholars
D) The analogy with fasting

Key Takeaway
A sajdat al-tilawa that becomes due during prayer must be performed in the prayer; if missed, the obligation lapses and is not performed outside.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Merging Pre-Prayer and In-Prayer Sajdat al-Tilawa
Rulings on merging pre-prayer and in-prayer sajdat al-tilawa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a sajdat al-tilawa is recited both before and during prayer, one prostration may suffice if the pre-prayer one was not performed, but if it was performed, a separate prostration is required for the prayer recitation.

Core Idea
A pre-prayer sajda without prostration merges with the in-prayer sajda, but a performed pre-prayer sajda does not exempt the prayer sajda.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: what happens if someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer, does not prostrate, then enters prayer and recites the same verse again? Or if he prostrated outside, then enters and recites again? The Hanafi ruling distinguishes two cases, based on whether the first sajda was actually performed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the concept of the stronger obligation subsuming the weaker.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Scenario 1: Person recites outside prayer, does not prostrate, then enters prayer and repeats the same verse. Scenario 2: Person recites and prostrates outside, then enters prayer and repeats.
The text: 'تلاها ثم شرع في الصلاة، وأعاد، كفته سجدة، وإن تلاها وسجد، ثم شرع فيها وأعادَ سَجَدَ أُخرى'.
2
Understand the Ruling for Scenario 1
One prostration suffices because the outside recitation created an obligation that was not yet fulfilled. When repeated in prayer, the prayer prostration (stronger) subsumes the outside obligation.
The first sajda is 'غير صلاتية' (non-prayer) and the second is 'صلاتية' (prayer). The stronger subsumes the weaker.
3
Understand the Ruling for Scenario 2
Two prostrations are required because the outside obligation was already fulfilled by prostrating. The prayer recitation creates a new, separate obligation that cannot merge with a completed act.
The first sajda was performed, so it does not become a follower.
4
Analyze the Legal Reasoning
The principle is that the prayer prostration has a 'complete obligation' (وجوب كامل) and the privilege of prayer, making it dominant. It can absorb an unfulfilled weaker obligation but not an already fulfilled one.
This is based on zahir al-riwayah.
5
Apply to Other Cases
If the outside recitation was in a different verse, each creates its own obligation; the ruling only applies to the same verse being repeated.
The text says 'أعاد' meaning he repeated the same verse.

كتاب الصلاة / سجود التلاوة. سمعها من إمام، ولم يدخل معه، أو دخل في ركعةٍ أُخرى سَجَدَ لا فيها، وإن دَخَلَ في تلك الركعة إن كان قبل سجودِ إمامِهِ سَجَدَ معه، والا لا يسجد، والسجدة الصلاتية لا تُقضَى خارجها. سمعها من إمام، ولم يدخل معه، أو دخل في ركعة أُخرى سَجَدَ لا فيها، وإن دَخَلَ في تلك الركعة إن كان: أي الدخول قبل سجودِ إمامِهِ سَجَدَ معه، والا لا يسجد. والسجدة الصلاتية لا تُقْضَى خارجها: أي سجدة التلاوة التي محلها الصلاة لا تُقضَى خارج الصلاة إلا إذا تابع المصلي التالي فتفسد لمتابعة غير إمامه، ولا تجزئه عما سمع. [١]قوله: سجد بعدها؛ أي بعد الفراغ عن الصَّلاة، هذا إذا ائتم به في الركعة الأخرى؛ لأن الواجب خارج الصَّلاة لا يقضى في الصَّلاة، وإذا لم يدخل معه فأداؤها ظاهر. [٢]قوله: وإلا لا يسجد؛ لأنه صار مدركاً لها بإدراك تلك الركعة. [٣] قوله: لا تُقضى؛ بصيغة المجهول، أي لا تؤدى فإنَّ القضاء يستعمل بمعنى الأداء، كما في قوله: فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلَوةُ فَانتَشِرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ. (٤) قوله: خارجها؛ قد يقال: إن سجدة التلاوة في الصَّلاةِ تتأدى بركوع وسجود صلبي عندنا فلا تبقى عليه حتى تؤدى خارج الصلاة. ويجاب عنه: بأنَّ هذا إنَّما هو إذا ركع وسجد بعد قراءة آية السجدة متصلاً من غير فصل بقدر ثلاث آيات، وأما إذا كان فصل، فلا تتأدى تلك السجدة بالركوع والسجود، فيلزم أن يبين حكمها هل تؤدى خارج الصَّلاةِ أم لا؟ والوجه في عدم أدائها خارج الصَّلاةِ أنَّ السَّجدة الصلوتية وجوبها كامل، ولها مزية الصَّلاة، ألا ترى أنه لو ضحك في سجدةِ التَّلاوة في الصلاة تنتقض طهارته، ولو ضحك فيها خارج الصَّلاةِ لا تنتقض، فتكون لها مزية فلا تتأدى بالناقص. [0] قوله: خارج الصَّلاة؛ سواء كان خارج الصَّلاةِ مطلقاً أو في صلاة أخرى. تلاها ثم شرع في الصلاة، وأعاد، كفته سجدة، وإن تلاها وسجد، ثم شرع فيها وأعادَ سَجَدَ أُخرى؛ لأنَّ في الصُّورة الأولى غير الصلاتية صارت تبعاً للصلاتية. [١] قوله: احتراز... الخ حاصله: أنه لو قلنا: وجبت في الصلاة يدخل فيها السجدة التي تجب في الصَّلاة، ومحل أدائها خارجها، كما إذا سمع المصلي ممن ليس معه، فيلزم أن تؤدى خارج الصَّلاة، مع أنه يلزم أداؤها خارجها. [٢] قوله: أو سمع من إمامه؛ أطلق لفظ الإمام باعتبار ما يؤول إليه، وإلا فهو ليس بإمـام له عندما سمعه منه. [٣] قوله: شرع... الخ؛ وفي عكسه؛ وهو ما إذا تلاها في الصَّلاةِ فسجد ثم أعادها بعد السلام، قيل: تجب أخرى، وقيل: لا، ووفق بينهما كحمل الأول على ما إذا تكلم؛ لأن الكلام يقطعُ حكم المجلس، والثاني على ما إذا لم يتكلم، وهذا هو الصحيح. [٤]قوله: وأعاد؛ أي قرأ تلك الآيةَ مرَّة أُخرى في الصلاة، فإن قرأ فيها آية أُخرى وجبت سجدة أخرى. [0] قوله: لأن... الخ؛ حاصله: أنَّ في الصورة الأولى، وهي ما إذا قرأ آية السجدة خارج الصَّلاة، ثم شرع في الصَّلاة وأعادها السجدة الأولى غير صلاتية، والثانية صلاتية، والأولى ناقصة بالنسبة إلى الثانية، وكون القوية الكاملة مستبعة للناقصة ممكن، فتصير الأولى تبعاً للثانية، وتتأدى بأدائها، وهذا كله على ظاهر الرواية.
Book of Prayer / Prostration of Recitation. He heard it from an imam and did not enter with him, or entered in another rak'ah, he prostrates not in it. And if he entered in that rak'ah, if it was before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him; otherwise he does not prostrate. The prayer prostration is not performed outside of it. He heard it from an imam and did not enter with him, or entered in another rak'ah, he prostrates not in it. And if he entered in that rak'ah, if the entry was before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him; otherwise he does not prostrate. 'The prayer prostration is not performed outside of it' means the prostration of recitation whose place is the prayer is not performed outside the prayer except if the praying person follows the reciter, then it is invalid due to following other than his imam, and it does not suffice him for what he heard. [1] His saying: 'he prostrates after it' means after finishing the prayer; this is if he followed him in the other rak'ah because the obligation outside prayer is not performed in prayer, and if he did not enter with him, its performance is apparent. [2] His saying: 'otherwise he does not prostrate' because he became a perceiver of it by perceiving that rak'ah. [3] His saying: 'is not performed' in the passive form, i.e., it is not done, for 'qada' is used in the meaning of 'ada', as in His saying: 'And when the prayer is concluded, disperse in the land'. [4] His saying: 'outside of it' it may be said: the prostration of recitation in prayer is fulfilled by the bowing and prostration of the prayer according to us, so it does not remain upon him to be performed outside prayer. The answer is: this is only if he bowed and prostrated immediately after reciting the verse of prostration without a gap of the length of three verses; but if there was a gap, then that prostration is not fulfilled by bowing and prostrating, so it is necessary to clarify its ruling: is it performed outside prayer or not? And the reason for not performing it outside prayer is that the prayer prostration has a complete obligation and has the privilege of prayer. Do you not see that if one laughs in the prostration of recitation in prayer, his ablution is nullified, but if he laughs in it outside prayer, it is not nullified? So it has a privilege, so it is not fulfilled by the deficient. [0] His saying: 'outside of it' includes both outside prayer absolutely or in another prayer. He recited it then entered into prayer and repeated it, one prostration suffices him; but if he recited it and prostrated, then entered into it and repeated it, he prostrates another because in the first case, the non-prayer one becomes a follower of the prayer one. [1] His saying: 'caution...' its summary is: if we say: 'it became obligatory in prayer', it includes the prostration that becomes obligatory in prayer and its place of performance is outside it, as when a praying person hears from someone not with him, then it would be necessary to perform it outside prayer, even though it is necessary to perform it outside it. [2] His saying: 'or heard from his imam' he used the term imam considering its ultimate outcome, otherwise he is not his imam when he heard from him. [3] His saying: 'entered...' and its opposite: when one recites it in prayer and prostrates, then repeats it after greeting: it is said another is obligatory, and it is said no; and reconciliation between them is made by carrying the first on the case where he spoke, because speech cuts the ruling of the session, and the second on the case where he did not speak, and this is the correct one. [4] His saying: 'and repeated' means he read that verse another time in prayer, for if he read another verse in it, another prostration becomes obligatory. [0] His saying: 'because...' its summary: in the first case, which is when one reads the verse of prostration outside prayer, then enters prayer and repeats it, the first prostration is non-prayer and the second is prayer, and the first is deficient relative to the second, and it is possible that the strong complete one subsumes the deficient, so the first becomes a follower of the second and is performed by its performance; and all this is according to the apparent transmission.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on rulings related to sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) when it is heard from an imam, and the distinction between prostration performed inside prayer versus outside. The text explains that if a person hears a verse of prostration from an imam but does not join his prayer, or joins in a different rak'ah, he should not prostrate within that rak'ah. However, if he joins that rak'ah before the imam performs the prostration, he prostrates with him. The key principle is that a prostration that was supposed to be performed in prayer is not made up outside of it. This is supported by the Quranic usage where 'qada' means 'to perform' (Surah al-Jumu'ah, ayah 10). The commentary addresses an objection that in prayer, the prostration of recitation is fulfilled by the regular bowing and prostration (ruk'u and sujud) and thus does not need to be performed outside. The response distinguishes this: it is only fulfilled if the worshiper bows and prostrates immediately after reciting the verse without a gap of more than three verses; otherwise, it is not fulfilled, and the ruling stands that it is not performed outside. The reasoning is that the prayer prostration has a complete obligation and the privilege of prayer (as shown by laughter nullifying ablution in prayer but not outside), so it cannot be performed with a deficient act like an outside prostration. The passage also covers a scenario: if someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer, then enters prayer and recites the same verse again, one prostration suffices because the outside one becomes subsidiary to the prayer one. But if he recites and prostrates outside, then in prayer recites again, he must perform another prostration because the outside one was already performed and cannot be merged. There is a noted disagreement (ikhtilaf) about the reverse case: if he recites in prayer, prostrates, then after salutation recites again; some say another prostration is required, others say not. The reconciliation is based on whether he spoke between recitations, which changes the ruling of the session. The text concludes that these rulings are on the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah).

Key Terms
تبع (taba'): Becoming a follower; the weaker obligation is subsumed by the stronger.
غير صلاتية (ghayr ṣalātiyyah): Non-prayer prostration; one that becomes due outside prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer and prostrates, then in prayer recites the same verse again, how many prostrations are due?
A) One – the outside prostration covers both.
B) Two – the outside one was already performed, so the prayer one is separate.
C) None – the prayer recitation does not require a prostration if the verse was already recited outside.
D) One – the prayer prostration subsumes the outside one.

Key Takeaway
When the same prostration verse is recited before and during prayer, one prostration suffices if the pre-prayer recitation was not yet prostrated; otherwise, separate prostrations are required.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
One Sujood for Repeated Tilawah Across Prayer Boundaries
Explains the ruling of sujood al-tilawah repeated across prayer boundaries with intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sajdah ayah is recited outside prayer and again inside prayer, and explain why one prostration suffices according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for repeated tilawah if the assembly is unified, even across prayer boundaries.

This lesson examines the ruling of sujood al-tilawah when the same verse of prostration is recited in different contexts – outside prayer and then inside prayer. The Hanafi school’s authoritative position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that one prostration suffices, provided the assembly (majlis) is considered one. However, a rare transmission (Nawadir) requires two prostrations. Understanding the rationale and the concept of assembly is key to applying this rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the act: reciting a sajdah ayah outside prayer, then reciting the same ayah again inside prayer. Determine if a prostration was performed outside or not.
Two subcases: (1) no external prostration, (2) external prostration performed.
2
State the two opinions
Zahir al-Riwayah: one prostration suffices when the assembly is unified. Nawadir: two prostrations required because prayer changes the assembly.
The difference hinges on whether prayer breaks the previous assembly of tilawah.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Zahir al-Riwayah argues that the stronger (prayer) prostration encompasses the weaker (external) one; the assembly remains one. Nawadir argues that the prayer creates a new assembly.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the concept of majlis.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Zahir al-Riwayah, as supported by the majority of later Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Marghinani, author of al-Nahr).
The Nawadir transmission is considered weak for fatwa.
5
Apply to variations
If the assembly is broken by speech or a significant break, even on Zahir al-Riwayah, two prostrations may be required. The passage reconciles differing reports based on whether speech occurred.
This shows the practical impact of the assembly concept.

He recited it, then began the prayer, and repeated it, one prostration suffices him. And if he recited it and prostrated, then began the prayer and repeated it, he prostrates another. I only said its place is the prayer, and I did not say 'the one that became obligatory in the prayer' as a precaution against what became obligatory in the prayer but whose place of performance is outside the prayer, such as when the prayer hears from someone not with him, or hears from his imam and follows him in another rak'ah. He said: 'Then he began the prayer, and repeated, one prostration suffices him. And if he recited and prostrated, then began and repeated, he prostrates another.' Because in the first scenario, the non-prayer one becomes a follower of the prayer one. Commentary on 'precaution': his summary: if we said 'it became obligatory in the prayer', it would include the prostration that becomes obligatory in the prayer but whose place of performance is outside it, as when the prayer hears from someone not with him – then it would be necessary to perform it outside the prayer, while it is necessary to perform it outside it. Commentary on 'hears from his imam': he used the term 'imam' considering what it will become, otherwise he is not his imam at the time he heard from him, and that example is not hidden; for when he heard the sajdah from the imam before his following and then followed him in another rak'ah, he is not one for whom it became obligatory in prayer; rather he is one for whom it became obligatory outside it, and its place of performance is also outside it. Commentary on 'he began...': and its opposite: if he recited it in the prayer and prostrated, then repeated it after the salam, it is said another is obligatory, and it is said no; and reconciliation is made by carrying the first upon the case if he spoke, because speech severs the rule of the assembly, and the second upon the case if he did not speak – this is correct, as in al-Nahr. Commentary on 'and repeated': i.e., he read that same ayah another time in the prayer; if he read another ayah, another prostration becomes obligatory. Commentary on 'because...': his summary: in the first scenario, i.e., when he read the sajdah ayah outside the prayer, then began the prayer and repeated it, the first prostration is non-prayer, the second is prayer, and the first is deficient relative to the second; and it is possible for the strong complete one to encompass the deficient one, so the first becomes a follower of the second and is fulfilled by its performance – all this according to al-Zahir al-Riwayah. (1) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq 1:341. Book of Prayer/ Sujood al-Tilawah: 297 'And if the assembly is not unified.' In the second scenario, when he prostrated before the prayer, it does not count for what became obligatory in the prayer at all. The wording of al-Mukhtasar: 'and if he repeats in one assembly, or in a prayer, one prostration suffices; and in the narration of al-Nawadir, one does not suffice him; and the source of the disagreement is whether the prayer changes the assembly or not?' as in al-Nahr. And if he did not prostrate in this scenario in the prayer, both are dropped; because the external one took the ruling of the prayer one, so it drops as a follower of it; and in the narration of al-Nawadir, it does not drop. Commentary on 'and if the assembly is not unified': the waw is for accompaniment; this is what many mentioned, like the author of al-Durar, al-Bada'i', al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and others; and the author of al-Bahr stipulated its unity, and similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Nihayah, and al-Tabyin, and others, and apparently there is disagreement in it. So said al-Khayr al-Ramli in his Hashiyat al-Bahr. And al-Shurnbulali made their statement 'even if the assembly differs' based on assuming the validity of the narration of al-Nawadir, that the assembly is changed by prayer judicially; because the assembly of prayer is different from the assembly of tilawah. As for al-Zahir, the assembly is united in reality and judicially. So if it were not united even judicially by an act other than prayer, the prayer one does not suffice for what came before it. Commentary on 'and the wording of al-Mukhtasar': he pointed by its mention to the fact that its expression is more concise and precise than the expression of the Matn, because it encompasses the previous and subsequent issues of the Matn, namely the sufficiency of one when the assembly is unified. (1) The expression in al-Nuqayah (p. 34): 'And if he repeats in one assembly, or prayer, one prostration suffices.' (2) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq 1:341. (3) Durar al-Hukkam 1:158. (4) al-Durr al-Mukhtar 1:114. (5) al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:134. (6) Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:207. (7) In Hashiyat Durar al-Hukkam 1:158.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling of sujood al-tilawah when the same ayah is recited twice – once outside prayer and once inside. It expands on the base text and discusses the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir. The author begins by stating the rule: if someone recites a sajdah ayah outside prayer, then begins prayer and recites the same ayah again, one prostration suffices for both. Similarly, if he recites it outside prayer and prostrates, then begins prayer and recites it again, he must prostrate again in prayer. The reason given is that the first (external) prostration becomes a follower (tabi') of the second (prayer) prostration, so the stronger (prayer) one encompasses the weaker one. This is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage then clarifies that the phrase 'its place is the prayer' refers to the obligation being tied to prayer, not the exact moment of obligation; there are cases where the obligation arises in prayer but the performance is outside, like hearing the ayah from someone not in the prayer or from an imam before joining. The commentary then discusses the opposite case: if one recites in prayer and prostrates, then recites again after salam, opinions differ. Reconciliation is made by considering whether speech (which breaks the assembly) occurred. The main dispute is over the effect of prayer on the unity of the assembly (majlis). According to Zahir al-Riwayah, entering prayer does not change the assembly; the external and internal recitations are considered one assembly, so one prostration suffices. According to Nawadir, prayer changes the assembly judicially, so two prostrations are required. The author cites al-Mukhtasar's wording which is more comprehensive, covering both the case of repetition in one assembly and in one prayer. The later scholars differ on whether unity of assembly is required; some, like the author of al-Bahr, stipulate it. The correct view, as per al-Nahr, is that if the assembly differs (even due to speech), the prayer prostration does not suffice for the external one. The passage ends with a note that al-Shurnbulali explained the 'different assembly' position as based on accepting the Nawadir narration.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujood al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran; its ruling is wajib in the Hanafi school.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmission of Imam Muhammad's six books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.), representing the official Hanafi position.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session or assembly in which a recitation occurs; its unity or change affects whether one prostration suffices for multiple recitations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, if someone recites a sajdah ayah outside prayer, then prays and recites the same ayah again in prayer, how many prostrations are required?
A) Two prostrations – one for each recitation
B) One prostration suffices for both
C) No prostration is required
D) Only the external one is required, not the internal one

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, one sujood al-tilawah can fulfill multiple recitations of the same verse if they occur in a single assembly, even if part is outside and part inside prayer.

One Prostration for Multiple Recitations? The Principle of Tadakhul in Sujud al-Tilawah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tadakhul in sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tadakhul in sujud al-tilawah and distinguish the Zahir al-Riwayah view from the Nawadir narration.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in the same sitting – istihsan overrides rigid qiyas.

When the same prostration verse is recited repeatedly in one sitting or prayer, is a separate prostration required each time? The Hanafi school addresses this through the principle of tadakhul (overlapping), favoring ease over strict analogy. This lesson unpacks the dispute between the mainstream Hanafi view and a rare narration, revealing how istihsan operates in fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and relied-upon ruling
Consider a person who recites the same prostration verse twice in one sitting without prostrating in between. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what is the ruling?
The core ruling: one prostration suffices for all recitations in the same sitting or prayer.
2
Recognize the opposing view
Identify the Nawadir narration that requires a separate prostration for each recitation. What reasoning does it rely on?
The opposing view is based on strict qiyas: each recitation is an independent cause for prostration.
3
Analyze the dispute’s hinge point
Understand that the disagreement centers on whether entering prayer changes the ‘majlis’ legally. How does each side define the majlis?
The Nawadir view holds that the prayer creates a new legal sitting; the majority view maintains the sitting is unified.
4
Examine the istihsan argument
See how the mainstream Hanafi view uses istihsan to override qiyas due to hardship. What evidence supports this?
Evidence includes the practice of Jibril and companions, who prostrated only once despite multiple recitations.
5
Apply the distinction between tadakhul in sabab vs. hukm
Distinguish whether the overlapping is in the cause (sabab) – making all recitations as one – or only in the ruling. How does this affect substitution for prostrations before and after?
If overlapping is in the sabab, one prostration substitutes for both past and future recitations; if only in the ruling, it only substitutes for past.

Thus mentioned by a group like the author of al-Durar, al-Bada'i', al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and others. The author of al-Bahr stipulated its unification, and similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Nihaya, al-Tabyin, and others. Apparently there is disagreement. Thus said al-Khayr al-Ramli in his Hashiya on al-Bahr. And al-Shurunbulali made their statement 'if the sitting differs' based on conceding to the Narration of al-Nawadir, namely that the sitting is changed by prayer legally, because the sitting of prayer is different from the sitting of recitation. As for the apparent view, the sitting is unified both in reality and legally. So if it were not unified, even legally by an action other than prayer, the prayer [recitation] would not suffice for what preceded it. His statement: 'And the wording of al-Mukhtasar' — he indicated by its mention that its expression is more concise and precise than the expression of the Matn because it encompasses the previous and subsequent issue of the Matn, which is the sufficiency of one when the sitting is unified. He repeated it in a sitting, one prostration suffices him — i.e., he recited outside of prayer then repeated it in prayer. And it is understood from the specification of the repeated [recitation] as being in prayer that the first was outside prayer. He repeated it in a sitting 'one prostration suffices him', and there is no difference between reading twice then prostrating, or reading and prostrating then reading it in that sitting. [Commentary on 'i.e. he recited']: He indicated by his interpretation that the intended meaning of 'repetition in prayer' is not that he recites it twice in prayer, but rather that the second is in prayer and the first is outside it. Hence the error of al-Barjandi becomes apparent, as he interpreted this in his commentary as repetition in prayer, which is an interpretation that the author would not be pleased with. His statement: 'it is understood... etc.' — it may be objected that just as one does not understand from the specification of the repeated [recitation] to the sitting that the first is not in the sitting, similarly one does not understand what he mentioned. His statement: 'a sitting... etc.' — performing it after the first is better, as in al-Qunyah, and in al-Bahr, delaying is more precautionary. His statement: 'the sitting' — the basis for this is that the prostration is built on overlapping (tadakhl) as istihsan, and by qiyas each recitation requires its own prostration. The reason for istihsan is hardship; indeed Muslims need to teach and learn the Quran, and they often need repetition, so requiring repetition leads to hardship, which is negated. This is supported by what is narrated that Jibril used to recite to the Prophet and his companions, and they would only prostrate once, and similarly from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, teacher of al-Hasan and al-Husayn. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah. This overlapping is an overlapping in the cause (sabab), by making all as one recitation on condition of unity of sitting and verse. Therefore one [prostration] substitutes for what preceded it and what follows it. If it were overlapping of the ruling only, it would only substitute for what preceded it.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Salah treats the ruling on sujud al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) when the same verse of prostration is recited multiple times. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute comparing the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwayah position with a rare narration (Nawadir). The opening statement establishes that if the sitting (majlis) is not unified, a prostration offered before prayer does not count for the obligation that arose during prayer. The core rule from al-Mukhtasar: if one repeats a prostration verse in a single sitting or within one prayer, one prostration suffices. However, in the Narration of al-Nawadir (transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad), one prostration does not suffice—each recitation requires its own prostration. The disagreement hinges on whether entering prayer changes the sitting: the Nawadir view holds that the prayer sitting is legally distinct from the recitation sitting, so prostrations do not overlap; the majority (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that the sitting remains unified in reality and law, so one prostration covers all recitations. The commentary then clarifies that the phrase 'repeated in prayer' refers to one recitation outside prayer and one inside, not two inside. A subtle objection is raised that the specification does not necessarily imply the first is outside, but the commentator dismisses this. The preferred practice (as in al-Qunyah) is to prostrate after the first recitation, though delaying is also precautionary. The underlying legal principle (asl) is to base the prostration on overlapping (tadakhl) by way of istihsan. Qiyas would require a separate prostration for each recitation, but istihsan overrides qiyas due to the hardship that would arise from constant repetition during Qur'anic teaching and learning. This istihsan is supported by the practice of Jibril reciting to the Prophet and companions prostrating only once, and by the practice of the great Qur'an teachers Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. Finally, the passage distinguishes two types of overlapping: overlapping in the cause (sabab)—where all recitations are treated as one, so a single prostration substitutes for both past and future recitations in that sitting—and overlapping in the ruling only, which would only substitute for past recitations. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah view: one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting or prayer.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
تداخل (tadākhul): Legal overlapping: treating multiple causes as one, so one act of worship suffices for all.
مجلس (majlis): The session or sitting during which recitation occurs; if repeated in the same physical or legal sitting, overlapping applies.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict qiyas to avoid hardship or to achieve a more equitable result.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), if someone recites the same prostration verse twice in one sitting without prostrating between them, how many prostrations are required?
A) Two prostrations, one for each recitation
B) One prostration suffices for both
C) No prostration is required
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations of the same prostration verse in one sitting or prayer, based on istihsan to avoid hardship.

One Prostration for Repeated Sajdah Recitation in One Sitting
Ruling on sufficing one prostration for repeated recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a sajdah verse in one sitting and explain the basis of tadakhul (overlapping) and istihsan.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for repeated recitation in one sitting due to tadakhul and juristic preference.

When a sajdah verse is recited multiple times in the same sitting, does each recitation demand its own prostration? The Hanafi school, prioritising ease in worship, rules that a single prostration fulfills the obligation for all. This lesson unpacks the principle of tadakhul (overlapping) and the proof from istihsan and prophetic practice that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (repeating a sajdah verse in one sitting) and the hukm (one prostration suffices).
The ruling applies whether the repetition occurs before or after prostrating, as long as the sitting (majlis) is the same.
2
Locate the dalil
The text uses istihsan (juristic preference) and a hadith about Jibril reciting to the Prophet and Companions prostrating only once.
The hadith is from the practice of the Companions, showing the Prophet's approval.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith demonstrates that multiple recitations did not require multiple prostrations, indicating the permissibility of merging. Istihsan overrides qiyas (that would require a prostration for each recitation) to avoid hardship.
The hardship (haraj) arises from frequent repetition in teaching and learning the Quran.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require separate prostrations as each recitation is a separate cause. The Hanafi position is based on tadakhul in the cause.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in a teaching setting, a Hanafi need only prostrate once, while a Shafi'i would prostrate for each recitation.

If he repeats it in a sitting, one prostration suffices him. That is, he recited outside of prayer, then repeated it in prayer. And it is understood from specifying the repeated one as being in prayer that the first was outside prayer. 'He repeated it in a sitting: one prostration suffices him' and there is no difference between reciting twice then prostrating, or reciting and prostrating, then reciting it again in that sitting. His statement: i.e., he recited; he indicated by his interpretation that what is meant by 'repeating in prayer' is not that he recites it twice in prayer, but that the other one is in prayer and the first is outside it.
